<div id="review_113155930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113155930" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369004887p2/2753251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113155930?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/2753251-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=arc-2011">arc-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=highly-anticipated">highly-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2753251-alyssa?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113155930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7410995256053708884">I adore Claudia Gray (a pseudo, in case you didn’t know), as both a person and a writer. I followed her blog up until it became the non-active type it is today, finding her to be sweet and generous, as well as incredibly personable and friendly. Her debut series, <i>Evernight</i>, is one of the only vampire texts that I can stomach nowadays, and trust me, that’s not a compliment I dish out to everyone. <br/><br/>The moment I’d heard she was working on something different, my excitement – as well as my guard – sh</span>
  <span id="freeText7410995256053708884" style="display:none">I adore Claudia Gray (a pseudo, in case you didn’t know), as both a person and a writer. I followed her blog up until it became the non-active type it is today, finding her to be sweet and generous, as well as incredibly personable and friendly. Her debut series, <i>Evernight</i>, is one of the only vampire texts that I can stomach nowadays, and trust me, that’s not a compliment I dish out to everyone. <br /><br />The moment I’d heard she was working on something different, my excitement – as well as my guard – shot up. Was I excited she was working on something new? Of course. Was I thrilled – and admittedly, a little nervous – that she was taking on the RMS Titanic as a scenery? Absolutely. Was I pleased with her description – for most of it, yes I was pleased.<br /><br />But little old anxious Alyssa just couldn’t stop fretting over one little detail: the werewolves. How could someone who wrote vampire fiction so fantastically fast forward to the other end of the spectrum, in turn to write of the creatures of the moon? How could someone who was so on top of the <i>me-drink-you-blood</i> party decide to write something so…different, risqué, overdone? Fret did I. Luckily, I was anxious for nothing.<br /><br />Claudia Gray eases her way by vampires and the States and ships herself across the ocean to London, England, where <i>Fateful</i> sets off. She focuses in on a very special ladies’ maid named Tess Davies, who simply wants to rid herself of the plights of serving others and wants to indulge in a new life in America. She leads us towards the RMS Titanic and introduces us to Alec, a boy with a secret and a disarming smile. And when she brings us to the end of what’s bound to be an unfortunate tale, she leaves us with feelings of both hope and grief over the very real event in which this book is involved in.<br /><br />I tried really hard to find something wrong with Tess and Alec. I took out my looking glass and I searched up and down the pages for what you’ll usually find in a YA paranormal these days: a desperate protagonist, a controlling love interest, a love triangle, a predictable plot. Fortunately, Gray has studied her paranormals and has taken a different approach in writing her own – what I found in <i>Fateful</i> was a bittersweet story complete with action, romance, political intrigue and a very sophisticated and well-tackled take on the tragedy that was the sinking of what had been considered “The Unsinkable.”<br /> <br />Although Tess could be considered judgmental and stuck-up, I understood that her attitude was based on her times’ society and her position as a ladies’ maid. Without much schooling, Tess still proved resourceful and intelligent, something I look for in heroines. The other characters were enjoyable reads, too. Alec was, to me, nothing special as a love interest, but he wasn’t an ass and he wasn’t too gentlemanly. He played the part of the werewolf – as did the Big Bad Wolf Mikhail – exceptionally well, especially since Gray’s take on werewolves was as twisted and captivating as her twist on vampires in her previously published books.<br /><br />The werewolf mythology in <i>Fateful</i> wasn’t anything like I’ve seen before, although I am a little sick of the whole creature in all. Please don’t mistake me, though: I don’t think Gray wrote <i>Fateful</i> with werewolves simply because it’s what’s in – I’m pretty sure it’s because she knows she writes paranormal well and because she wanted to add something sure to her tackling of the Titanic tragedy. Gray, although placing some annoying stereotypes in – I hate that automatically rich people are considered snobs and the epitomes of rudeness – her writing was stunning and worthy of my envy and fascination.*<br /><br />The novel could have so easily could have sunk. The Titanic is a pretty large thing to tackle, something pretty monumental and real. Since it truly existed and sunk, its case being one of the most popular – and unfortunate – disasters in history books, it would have been very easy to find Gray’s twist on the story distasteful and wrongly executed. Gray states her research was extensive in the Authors Note, and truthfully? I thought she very wrote a stunning story. It tackled love, it tackled tragedy, it tackled a powerful storyline. As beautifully rendered Cameron’s film of the historical event, Gray has written a novel that will touch many readers to smiles and tears.<br /><br />4.25/5<br /><br /><i>*I may not have werewolf senses, but I certainly smell the opening and possibility for a sequel to <i>Fateful<i>, something I’m not sure I support or don’t care for.<br /><br />I was provided my ARC copy from the publisher. Thank you to HarperCollinsCA and HarperTeen for the review copy.</i></i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7410995256053708884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17271097523290290057">The best part about the book--and the sole reason it gets 4 stars--is the almost-ending. I'm not going to put it under a spoiler tag, because everyone should know this already, but man, I could not stop crying when the ship was starting to sink, and Tessa was describing how there weren't enough lifeboats, and the overall feel when fifteen hundred people know they're about to die. <br/>It's heartbreaking, really. I think that was the thing that made me cry during the James Cameron Titanic. Not Jack an</span>
  <span id="freeText17271097523290290057" style="display:none">The best part about the book--and the sole reason it gets 4 stars--is the almost-ending. I'm not going to put it under a spoiler tag, because everyone should know this already, but man, I could not stop crying when the ship was starting to sink, and Tessa was describing how there weren't enough lifeboats, and the overall feel when fifteen hundred people know they're about to die. <br />It's heartbreaking, really. I think that was the thing that made me cry during the James Cameron Titanic. Not Jack and Rose, but the hundreds of people that were going to die. And it really hits hard, since it actually happened. This may be a work of fiction, but it was still based off a tragic historical event. <br /><br />The romance is shoddy, and completely insta-love, but I think it's worth enduring to get to the meat of the story with the werewolves and the Brotherhood. </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1044447701?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=2-and-a-half-stars">2-and-a-half-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1044447701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11416960400526330558">Interesting Titanic retelling.<br/><br/>Here are some of my thoughts:<br/>•	I liked the romance, but would have preferred more developments, instead of them mainly fixated on the usual problems. However, it was different that the author made the guy into a werewolf.<br/>•	I loved, loved Alec’s dad, who only wanted the best for his son. He was a thoroughly good guy, and I appreciated that he had no problem with Tess’ social status, and just wanted them to be happy.<br/>•	The friendship b/w Tess and Irene was surprisingly</span>
  <span id="freeText11416960400526330558" style="display:none">Interesting Titanic retelling.<br /><br />Here are some of my thoughts:<br />•	I liked the romance, but would have preferred more developments, instead of them mainly fixated on the usual problems. However, it was different that the author made the guy into a werewolf.<br />•	I loved, loved Alec’s dad, who only wanted the best for his son. He was a thoroughly good guy, and I appreciated that he had no problem with Tess’ social status, and just wanted them to be happy.<br />•	The friendship b/w Tess and Irene was surprisingly nice. Irene was SUCH a sweet character. I did not expect her to stand up for Tess who was a servant repeatedly to her narcissistic mother.<br />•	The other friend she made (forgot her name) was thorny, but the dynamic between the two was affectionate and it was great they were there for each other in time of need.<br />•	I have to admit that the usual problems with naggy rich people and abusive werewolf villain were redundant at times. However, when the iceberg scene came, I was holding my breath. It really made me feel for the characters, even ones that only got one sentence mentioned, because of obviously how sad the event was. <br /><br />Overall, unique interpretation of Titanic. There could have been more developments with the romance, but it was nice. It was slow a times, but I thought the scenes later on when the iceberg hit were done well, and definitely had an emotional impact. <b>3 stars (maybe 2.5)</b><br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bittersweet, but happy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for main characters, sad for side characters <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, no, medium <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Didn’t cry but sad <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scenes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The scene where the deaths from the Titanic made them realize any reasons or hesitations of not being together were silly and they should be together when they can. The ending with them planning for their future and living in a cozy home together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_122209799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122209799" />
    <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten"><img alt="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305870184p2/2406353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122209799?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten">Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780732294281" href="/book/show/12516676-fateful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=harper-collins-sent">harper-collins-sent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=publisher-sent">publisher-sent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=signed-copies">signed-copies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer122209799&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122209799" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12661203690419256663"><i>*Firstly, thank-you to Harper Collins Australia for sending me a copy of this book to review*</i><br/><br/>Fateful caught me from the beginning. It took me on an incredible journey of love, danger and tragedy. It made my heart soar before breaking it as I knew it eventually would, only to have it heal me once again and leave me with endless hope. <br/>There’s no denying that the story of the Titanic isn’t a powerful one. It has been ever since the beginning, and in this book Claudia Gray creates a tale that transp</span>
  <span id="freeText12661203690419256663" style="display:none"><i>*Firstly, thank-you to Harper Collins Australia for sending me a copy of this book to review*</i><br /><br />Fateful caught me from the beginning. It took me on an incredible journey of love, danger and tragedy. It made my heart soar before breaking it as I knew it eventually would, only to have it heal me once again and leave me with endless hope. <br />There’s no denying that the story of the Titanic isn’t a powerful one. It has been ever since the beginning, and in this book Claudia Gray creates a tale that transports you to another time and place. It’s beautiful and romantic, but hauntingly tragic as events come to pass that we all know are inevitable even before reading this tale.<br /><br />Going into this book I knew that it would have to end it pain at some point; that many of the characters we met on the ship wouldn’t survive that tragic night, but that didn’t stop me from loving them regardless. Born to a time of high class and wealth, where difference of importance was a common thing, all these characters were captivating and wonderful. Some were well bred, but still kind as we saw with Miss Irene. Others were born to a lower class, yet still strong as individuals and soul as we saw with kind George, sweet Ned, feisty Myriam and honourable Mr Marlowe who loved his son no matter what. Of course there were the cruel ones as we saw with Lady Regina, Layton and Mikhail, but they gave the book a strong foundation and made it seem more realistic to that time. Each and every character had their own story aboard the Titanic and their own past that made them such colourful characters to read about. <br /><br />Tess was a great lead to read about. She came from humble beginnings, and she was just a normal servant girl from those times who happened to want more from life. She knows her place in life and who she is, but she wanted the freedom that only fleeing her employer could give and believed the Titanic was her ticket to that. One of the things I loved about Tess was that she was so normal; of course she had vulnerabilities and she was scared but she was strong too. I thought she reacted to learning about werewolves with a healthy amount of fear, but she saw them in a good and balanced light over time and none of that changed her growing feelings for Alec. <br />As for Mr. Alec Marlowe....swoon. What can I say? Born to wealth, he was haunted by what he was now was and the things he did. He’s just the kind of man a girl can dream would sweep her off her feet in those times and days. He was a nobleman, but none of that mattered to him when it came to Tess. He treated those around him who weren’t quite in the same position as he was with respect too. He was sexy and charming and fell completely in love with Tess, eventually making a selfless act that would save her life. <br /><br />Despite the events of the Titanic, or perhaps even because I knew how it would end, the relationship between Tess and Alec was so romantic! Both were so different, and from different classes, but the sparks between them were beautiful and their relationship was passionate and real. It was refreshing to have Alec’s family support his romance with a woman of a lower class and to have them have his father’s blessing. It was nice not having this as an obstacle for them and instead seeing them face a completely different threat. Tess and Alec connected and had a bond that nothing—not what he was, not difference of status, not even the ocean itself--could break. It was pure and so intense to read about. <br /><br />I’d be lying if I didn’t mention that some scenes, especially towards the ending of this book, had me very emotional. When you love certain characters and follow them on their journey, only to have it end in such a tragic, be it inevitable way, it’s very sad. I can see the beauty in the way Claudia Gray has written the tale and her characters and I’m so pleased to have read their story. <br />It was impossible not to get swept up in this intense, passionate tale and I held on through it all; unable to stop reading as the characters found their feet and each other. The pain and sadness of the ending didn’t over power the hope and promise found at the very, <i>very</i> end and it was equal balance happiness and tragedy. <br /><br />This book is an incredible journey that will draw all number of emotions from readers and will stay with you, long after you turn the last page! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12661203690419256663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161456244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161456244" />
    <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids"><img alt="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319228268p2/4397975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161456244?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids">Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062006202" href="/book/show/10429017-fateful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2011-release">2011-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2011-100-book-challenge">2011-100-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=mundie-moms-reviews">mundie-moms-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161456244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17518498186731733615">A compelling story with an enticing paranormal romance, an engaging story line and a beautiful retelling of the heartbreaking tragedy of the Titanic, Fateful is a book that I sat and devoured in one sitting. Claudia Gray has written a story that is captivating, well researched and incredibly written. <br/><br/>Aside from being a paranormal story, I loved the historical part of Fateful. Claudia did a brilliant job with her detailed writing and how she handled the entire voyage of the Titanic. Even though I</span>
  <span id="freeText17518498186731733615" style="display:none">A compelling story with an enticing paranormal romance, an engaging story line and a beautiful retelling of the heartbreaking tragedy of the Titanic, Fateful is a book that I sat and devoured in one sitting. Claudia Gray has written a story that is captivating, well researched and incredibly written. <br /><br />Aside from being a paranormal story, I loved the historical part of Fateful. Claudia did a brilliant job with her detailed writing and how she handled the entire voyage of the Titanic. Even though I knew what was going to happen, I was so engaged with the romance, the paranormal twists and everything else that was happening, that my worries and fears for who would survive subsided until the moment the ship hits the ice burg. Claudia threw in some fabulous twists that kept this story well paced and kept me hooked until the very end. I thoroughly enjoyed being taken back in time and feeling as though I was aboard the Titanic with this great cast of characters. <br /><br />There's few books that I read and end up enjoying most every character I read about, and Fateful is one of them. Claudia's characters are so well written, in-depth, and despite some of them being paranormals, they felt believable to me. It wasn't hard for me to fall in love with some of the main characters and even the secondary characters, as they were easy to imagine, and even the villain was easy to despise. He was so well written. Talk about a fabulous evil guy. <br /><br />The story is centered on Tess, a servant girl from England who's traveling with the family she works for to the US. I really admired Tess's strength. She's had to deal with a lot of crap in her life, but that doesn't stop her from wanting to fulfill her dreams. In fact it makes her that much more determined to follow them. Tess inadvertently finds herself in the middle of a world she had no idea existed, and that puts her life in grave danger. Her reactions to some of the events that unfold aboard the Titanic are really credible. I'd be in state of shock if I found myself witnessing some of the things she does as well.<br /><br />The romance is so awesome! I love a well written time period romance. I really enjoyed the way Claudia developed the relationship between Alex and Tess. It's not a rushed, instant love kind of romance, but a well thought out, well written one that develops through out the course of the book. Alex is such a fabulous love interest. He's a tortured soul, but in a way that I totally understood why. He and Tess really bring out the best in each other. There romance is so addicting, I couldn't get enough of it! The sacrifices they make for each other totally made me cry! Not that I didn't except to cry since the story is set on the Titanic. <br /><br />Fateful has the perfect blend of historical references, romance and paranormal activity that fans of Claudia Gray, romance, history and paranormal books will really enjoy this one. I am in love with this book and it's ending is fabulous! I'm not sure if this is going to be a series or have a sequel, but whether it's a stand alone or not, this is a book I highly recommend picking up. There is some very mild language and an implied sexual scene. This is a book I'd recommend to readers 13 yrs &amp; older.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17518498186731733615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_172811688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172811688" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3448004-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277333038p2/3448004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172811688?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/3448004-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maria by: </span>
      Claudia Gray @ BookExpo
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172811688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13189968267316143079">Claudia Gray has to be one of my favorite authors, period. She just has this way of writing that makes you never want to put a book down. Of course, most of you have read the Evernight series (and if you haven't, you should go do so right now!), and so you know how amazing Claudia's novels are. But this one, Fateful, has made it's way to the top of my list.<br/><br/>I think one of the best aspects of Fateful is that you already know one thing that's going to happen - I mean, they're on the Titanic - we al</span>
  <span id="freeText13189968267316143079" style="display:none">Claudia Gray has to be one of my favorite authors, period. She just has this way of writing that makes you never want to put a book down. Of course, most of you have read the Evernight series (and if you haven't, you should go do so right now!), and so you know how amazing Claudia's novels are. But this one, Fateful, has made it's way to the top of my list.<br /><br />I think one of the best aspects of Fateful is that you already know one thing that's going to happen - I mean, they're on the Titanic - we all know how that ends up! Knowing that at any moment, they're going to hit the iceberg, knowing that the ship is going to sink, makes the story incredibly exciting before you even turn the first page. And I'd just like to add that even though the story takes place on the Titanic, the story is actually loosely based on the events of that day. Claudia takes great care to respect the memory of those who died.<br /><br />Now, on to the story. Immediately, I fell in love with our main character, Tess. She's sweet, generous, and kick-ass! She knows her place in life (as a servant), but at the same time, she's never afraid to step past her boundaries when she has to. At one point in the story, she even gets all dressed up and hangs out on the First Class deck of the ship - if that's not gutsy, I don't know what it is.<br /><br />I also fell in love with our paranormal hero in the story - Alec (although I do feel that this name is being over-used). In such a short novel, we learn that Alec is a werewolf (not by choice) and is refusing to become evil/greedy like all the other werewolves he knows. He'd actually rather die than join their cause, and that just makes us swoon even more. He's handsome, charming, and falls for the servant girl - how could you NOT love him!<br /><br />I will say no more - but I will tell you that this book is a must-read! The supsense, the action, the drama, the Titanic!!! Honestly...I wish it had been longer, lol. <br /><br />5 out of 5 stars!<br />Maria @GoodChoiceReading.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="13189968267316143079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13493876014553526190"><b>To be more accurate, I would like to rate this a 3.5!</b><br/><br/>Okay, I'm pretty fascinated by the Titanic incident back in 1912. I've researched quite a lot on it. I've watched Titanic 17394840 times (the reason behind it being that it came on HBO so many times). I'm also fascinated by werewolves. So when Gray smashed these two together, I went ballistic. <br/><br/>I was just like... <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360299i/711168._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>MAD.</b><br/><br/>Gray did a fantastic job with her research regarding the different classes on the Titanic. She did amazingly well on demonstratin</span>
  <span id="freeText13493876014553526190" style="display:none"><b>To be more accurate, I would like to rate this a 3.5!</b><br><br>Okay, I'm pretty fascinated by the Titanic incident back in 1912. I've researched quite a lot on it. I've watched Titanic 17394840 times (the reason behind it being that it came on HBO so many times). I'm also fascinated by werewolves. So when Gray smashed these two together, I went ballistic. <br><br>I was just like... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360299i/711168._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>MAD.</b><br><br>Gray did a fantastic job with her research regarding the different classes on the Titanic. She did amazingly well on demonstrating the lives of servants and first class passengers. Her descriptions, word choices, and timing were almost perfect. It was like walking through a field of flowers. I thoroughly enjoyed it. <br><br>Alec's descriptions were fantastic at first. However, every time he approached Tess, all she could think of were his "chestnut curls." I mean, his descriptions CAN go beyond that. What else? It was repetitive! <br><br>So I loved the writing, I loved the characters, I loved the concept of mixing Titanic and werewolves. So why did I rate it a 3.5? Because the whole "You make me human" thing is cliche. I didn't like it. At some points, I knew what was going to happen next. Alec saves Tess. He's the werewolf, blah blah blah. Nothing new. Also I felt like I could have known more about Tess. Some of her physical descriptions besides being tall and blonde. I would have liked to know more about her family. I also skipped some pages here and there. I couldn't help it. I just wasn't as interested as I was at the beginning of the book. However, I feel like I understand the basic plot of it. <br><br>Anyway, good book! <br><br>By the way: The cover for this version is so gorgeous! The other one was okay... Meh. </span>

<div id="review_206965474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206965474" />
    <a title="Kaysi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4105443-kaysi"><img alt="Kaysi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345951123p2/4105443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206965474?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaysi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaysi" href="/user/show/4105443-kaysi">Kaysi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780732294281" href="/book/show/12516676-fateful">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4105443-kaysi?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer206965474&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206965474" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17956174814892333179">I am bordering on 4.5 for this book.<br/><br/>Okay, I will be the first to admit it... I had reservations about this book. It had nothing to do with Claudia Gray, or werewolves, or RMS Titanic ... I quite like all of those (well I like Claudia, like reading about werewolves and like the history of the Titanic), I just was not sure about the combination of all those things.<br/><br/>I have always liked Claudia’s writing, but I must say, I liked this one the best. She done an amazing job of using old school language </span>
  <span id="freeText17956174814892333179" style="display:none">I am bordering on 4.5 for this book.<br /><br />Okay, I will be the first to admit it... I had reservations about this book. It had nothing to do with Claudia Gray, or werewolves, or RMS Titanic ... I quite like all of those (well I like Claudia, like reading about werewolves and like the history of the Titanic), I just was not sure about the combination of all those things.<br /><br />I have always liked Claudia’s writing, but I must say, I liked this one the best. She done an amazing job of using old school language and combined it with great stories – both real and fictional.<br /><br />Her story was compelling, and even over a short timeframe, the love and passion was there. There was a good combination of good and bad characters. There was a great display of the relationships and status of that era. I was very impressed with it all!!! Actually, the only thing I could say I was a bit unsure about was the amount of “relationships” between upper and lower class – I know they happened.. I know some of them were love, whilst some were merely using servants for personal pleasure, but I am unsure if it was quite that common (from Tess’s POV, there was her’s, Irene and Ned and somewhat between Myriam and George). For the characters I love loved (Tess, Alec, Mr. Marlowe, Irene, Ned, Myriam, George) there were characters I hated equally as much (Mikhail, Lady Regina, Layton), and when I say hate, you could really hate these characters! I think hating a character is a far stronger compliment to a writer than liking one – but that’s just me.<br /><br />I loved the characters – even the nasty ones... and some of them were extremely vile! Mickhail was the embodiment of evil, in the monster form, and on the other side, Lady Regina was a monster as well. Tess, whilst knowing her place, has a strong will and will not let go of her dreams... she won’t let her will to be broken. Very rare these days in YA books I liked how Claudia brought the whole werewolf thing in right from the beginning. Some authors drag the “reveal” out a little too much for my liking, but, she chucked it right in there.<br /><br />Alec, of course, was a great character. I liked how he saved her, then warned her to stay away from him directly after – numerous times. It showed that he does care, and that he is fully aware of how dangerous he is. He didn’t go down the line of being a jerk, which can quite often happen, but he did try to put the distance between them (without watching her sleep at night).<br /><br />I loved all the detail she put in regarding the Titanic itself, Claudia done a wonderful job of creating the “visual” for the readers. I am also impressed how she blurred the line between fact and fiction. She certainly done her research! And her description of the sinking – how wonderfully yet terrifyingly written. It contained wonderful descriptions of everything from people ignoring the warnings, not enough life-boats, lights going out and the actual breaking of the Titanic. I could clearly see that Alec was going to throw Tess overboard.. and the description of that fall was very vivid in my mind. But I must admit, it was Alec explaining that his dad decided to stay that really got to me.<br /><br />Now, the main reason I read this book was to see how Claudia would end it (besides the very pretty Australian cover). I mean really, where can she go with it? It’s the Titanic... it sinks, and it can only happen one way!!! Claudia impressed me!. It’s very sad that Irene, Ned, George and Mr. Marlowe did not make it off... but let’s face it... not everyone can survive!!! But I was more than happy to see Mikhail, Lady Regina, Layton stay on board!<br /><br />Afterwards, I was mainly eager to find out about Mikhail... and besides the very morbid scene where he returns – all I could think was – that means Alec survived! And then my next thought.... oh no.... will this be a series????? Of course I am happy that Tess and Alec get to be together... but there an opportunity for another book, after all, the Brotherhood is still after Alec.... but, the way it ended, I am personally happy to leave it there.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17956174814892333179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169095832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169095832" />
    <a title="Ashley - The Bookish Brunette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4407857-ashley---the-bookish-brunette"><img alt="Ashley - The Bookish Brunette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355409003p2/4407857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169095832?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley - The Bookish Brunette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley - The Bookish Brunette" href="/user/show/4407857-ashley---the-bookish-brunette">Ashley - The Bookish Brunette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4407857-ashley---the-bookish-brunette?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4407857-ashley---the-bookish-brunette?shelf=2011-release">2011-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169095832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17289043702926732413">WEREWOLVES? On the TITANIC??? Epic win!<br/><br/>Tess and Alec... no matter which way I look at it, or turn it around in my head- their relationship never felt REAL to me! I was never convinced of either of their feelings for the other. They fall "in love" like *BAM*, after a series of less than pleasant meetings and there is nothing supporting it!<br/><br/>Their relationship does become more plausible as the book continues, but only because we're more invested in the story and the characters! There was still never</span>
  <span id="freeText17289043702926732413" style="display:none">WEREWOLVES? On the TITANIC??? Epic win!<br /><br />Tess and Alec... no matter which way I look at it, or turn it around in my head- their relationship never felt REAL to me! I was never convinced of either of their feelings for the other. They fall "in love" like *BAM*, after a series of less than pleasant meetings and there is nothing supporting it!<br /><br />Their relationship does become more plausible as the book continues, but only because we're more invested in the story and the characters! There was still never any real basis for WHY she was suddenly so in love with him.<br /><br />The several subplots in Fateful were VERY well done, and very, very exciting! The noble family of Lisle... PENNILESS! Their son and heir impregnating a lowly servant girl, and letting his parents cast her out to starve! Their meek and timid, but kind daughter in love with someone she can never have... These were FLAWLESS and I loved every second of them!<br /><br />George and Myriam... I'd have LOVED to hear more about them!!! George is an officer on the ship and Myriam is a third class passenger, their insta-love connection NEVER felt forced! It was sweet, romantic and as simple as "hello". *sigh*<br /><br />You know... it's not like I didn't KNOW how this story would end. Obviously, the Titanic sinks... it's still terribly tragic! Gray does a beautiful job of recreating these terrifying and heartbreakingly sad moments,<br /><br /> "As I look past him and realize there are no more lifeboats close by, I wonder if we've found each other too late."<br /><br /> "Won't you tell Myriam- I'm sorry not to have had more time with her." -George (my poor, sweet George)<br /><br /> "When she takes my hand, I know it's all been real- all of it- and the horror is even more powerful than the fact that I've survived." -Tess<br /><br />I had finally been completely won over by this story- I'm talking 4.5 stars, only knocking the .5 because of my initial reservations toward Alec and Tess.When I got to the very last few pages, I was completely disappointed! My heart was breaking into 1000 pieces (which is good... I'm feeling EMOTION for Tess, finally!) and NO, I'm NOT going to tell you how it ends!<br /><br />I have NO doubt in my mind that a lot of people will probably love this ending- I, on the other hand was not a fan. So after much deliberation... 4 STARS!<br /><br /> • • • • • • • • • <br /><br /> And HOW freaking gorgeous is the new cover?! I absolutely LOVE it, the crimson dress she wore the day her and Alec had their date... her BLONDE hair (I wondered who the brunette chick was on the other cover!), the ice, the moon... everything is perfect! I loved the other one, but this cover is FAR more suited to the book!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17289043702926732413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_746378198" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/746378198" />
    <a title="Rachmi " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3047938-rachmi"><img alt="Rachmi " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358842498p2/3047938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/746378198?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachmi " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachmi " href="/user/show/3047938-rachmi">Rachmi </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047938-rachmi?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746378198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5339426333208334193">Before:<br/><br/>I have this book for a while but always skip it to read another books. The blurb quite interesting but I don't feel I want to read it soon since its setting is based on original story. Who is in this earth never heard of Titanic? So I was kind of feel there will be nothing new in it moreover it's about werewolves. One of paranormal themes that is quite popular now. Those reasons make it less appealing to me, though it has a very good rating here. But I finally picked it up for the sake of</span>
  <span id="freeText5339426333208334193" style="display:none">Before:<br /><br />I have this book for a while but always skip it to read another books. The blurb quite interesting but I don't feel I want to read it soon since its setting is based on original story. Who is in this earth never heard of Titanic? So I was kind of feel there will be nothing new in it moreover it's about werewolves. One of paranormal themes that is quite popular now. Those reasons make it less appealing to me, though it has a very good rating here. But I finally picked it up for the sake of reading challenge.<br /><br />After:<br /><br />At the beginning of the story, I was less impressed by Tess Davies, the main character and the narrator of the story. I think she's a bit too chatty for my taste and quite noisy in the monologue. She seems rather talks about herself than describe the worldbuiling to me. But, its fast-paced make me look forward for her adventure. It's like her servant description is enough as the introduction and allow the main story to take the center stage from chapter one. However, I didn't feel it loses pace for detail and description, as I often read in not-so-good fast-paced stories. Tess’s voice is so clear I can feel the atmosphere of how life in early 1900s was and her role as a servant. The more I read it the more I want to know it.<br /><br />There are barely surprises in it yet it can still make my heart beats fast. The hide and seek between Tess and Mikhail, the antagonist, is so good, in some part I really wanted to scream at her to run away and seek help. Knowing when Titanic will sink make it worse (in a good way, of course) it's like I was counting for the worse to happen to Tess and Alec and told them that nothing is matter at April 15th. And when it happened, I thought I won't have problem reading it since I've watched Titanic by James Cameron countless times, but then once again I was wrong. I can still feel it, the sadness and hopeless that Tess and other characters feel.<br /><br />As for the romance, I love the way Tess and Alec build their relationship. It surely is an insta-love but the one that I can say as my exception since I'm not an insta-love fan. Although they build it slowly in a short time if it is possible, they relationship feels natural and believable to me. They both have strong-will to face their problem and have each other back I think that's what I like most about them.<br /><br />In the end I think I should thank to the reading challenge for 'forced' me to read it. I loved and enjoyed it very much. It's definitely one of my favorite YA werewolves stories.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5339426333208334193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222706843" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222706843?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-ebook">own-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222706843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17157972811269055187">This might be more of a <b>3.5/5</b>. I'm not a big <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1192311.Claudia_Gray' title='Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>Claudia Gray</a> fan, but this was better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_' title='Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evernight</a>. I always feel distanced from her characters. But I cried so much in this! I have always had a soft spot for the Titanic. For as long as I can remember, its just so sad! But I am glad the actual sinking took up a small part of the book compared to the movie 'Titanic', where the sinking pretty much took up the last half of the movie. I wouldnt have been able to deal with that much crying.<br/><br/>The story wa</span>
  <span id="freeText17157972811269055187" style="display:none">This might be more of a <b>3.5/5</b>. I'm not a big <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1192311.Claudia_Gray" title="Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Claudia Gray</a> fan, but this was better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_" title="Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Evernight</a>. I always feel distanced from her characters. But I cried so much in this! I have always had a soft spot for the Titanic. For as long as I can remember, its just so sad! But I am glad the actual sinking took up a small part of the book compared to the movie 'Titanic', where the sinking pretty much took up the last half of the movie. I wouldnt have been able to deal with that much crying.<br /><br />The story was really interesting, involving werewolves and Mikhail added a lot of extra danger and suspense, and I liked the setting of a ship, although it could have been any ship. Tess and Alec were sweet of course, but their relationship felt a bit rushed. The first time they kissed I thought, "Already?" I know she only had a few days to work with on the Titanic, but Gray could have still added more scenes to each day in order for it to feel like longer before they kissed. Writers warp time all the time. But I cant complain about anything else. Tess and Alec had all the major points I would want in a YA romance. Lots of great kisses, self-sacrifice, a sex scene, and a happy ending.<br /><br />I'm not too upset that there isnt a sequel, but if there was I would definitely read it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17157972811269055187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qn9p1YOtPf/yJBp6Gyagqznx0s07btWUg0r6uiBw+SEcam7LRJNyj4+wXE/ZGI/PbRMcQdv6GFSUZwJBoCtoJA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+qWUNs90GCHfkjYzR7Ek3mgChfp8GklmDJmGEbkoLRVMsJMoCEpXUaIGcAaFjwu6POBLdpyOhKYbtH7qOXO8EA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer17088688299088580384">Claudia Gray is not my real name. I didn't choose a pseudonym because my real name is unpleasant (it isn't), because I'd always dreamed of calling myself this (I haven't) or even because I'm hiding from the remnants of that international diamond-smuggling cartel I smashed in 2003 (Interpol has taken care of them). In short, I took a pseudonym for no real reason whatsoever. Sometimes this is actual</span>
  <span id="freeText17088688299088580384" style="display:none">Claudia Gray is not my real name. I didn't choose a pseudonym because my real name is unpleasant (it isn't), because I'd always dreamed of calling myself this (I haven't) or even because I'm hiding from the remnants of that international diamond-smuggling cartel I smashed in 2003 (Interpol has taken care of them). In short, I took a pseudonym for no real reason whatsoever. Sometimes this is actually the best reason to do things.<br /><br />I live in New Orleans. So far, in life, I've been a disc jockey, a lawyer, a journalist and an extremely bad waitress, just to name a few. I especially like to spend time traveling, hiking, reading and listening to music. More than anything else, I enjoy writing. <br /></span>
